<div id="review_575793350" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/575793350" />
    <a title="David H." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18844431-david-h"><img alt="David H." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551048918p2/18844431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/575793350?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David H." class="user" itemprop="url" name="David H." href="/user/show/18844431-david-h">David H.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18844431-david-h?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer575793350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18150631452458530152">We get another time jump from the ending of the last book, this time about ten years. Aside from the Mage Wars trilogy written with Dixon, this is probably one of the few Valdemar trilogies with significant time jumps between books. But that makes sense in that Lackey is telling a story to cover the life of a legend whose fate we already know from the beginning of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13986.Arrows_of_the_Queen__Heralds_of_Valdemar___1_' title='Arrows of the Queen (Heralds of Valdemar, #1) by Mercedes Lackey' rel='nofollow noopener'>Arrows of the Queen</a>. I thought the author did a great job of setting up the temporal differences between Vanyel's and Talia's times i</span>
  <span id="freeText18150631452458530152" style="display:none">We get another time jump from the ending of the last book, this time about ten years. Aside from the Mage Wars trilogy written with Dixon, this is probably one of the few Valdemar trilogies with significant time jumps between books. But that makes sense in that Lackey is telling a story to cover the life of a legend whose fate we already know from the beginning of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13986.Arrows_of_the_Queen__Heralds_of_Valdemar___1_" title="Arrows of the Queen (Heralds of Valdemar, #1) by Mercedes Lackey" rel="nofollow noopener">Arrows of the Queen</a>. I thought the author did a great job of setting up the temporal differences between Vanyel's and Talia's times in a way that didn't annoy me. One thing that also really helped was the introduction of Stefen's character in this volume, as he's a great contrast to the gloomy Vanyel we've had this entire trilogy.<br /><br />The ending did feel <i>slightly</i> rushed (the sudden detour with the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[kyree <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> honestly seemed a bit awkward unless she's setting up something I don't remember yet for a later series). But the battle and the epilogue were just fantastic in the end.</span>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2457561444" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16868295942971045289">Sigh. As the final Act of an epic storyline, this novel was, in a word, disappointing.<br/><br/>Plot-wise, it was anticlimactic, and utilized a literary device I particularly dislike: <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[setting up the climax, and then cutting away to the POV of another character, who arrives on the scene only to witness the aftermath. <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/>Character-wise, I enjoyed the character of Stef, but felt he lacked depth. The interactions between him and Vaneyl were well written, and believable, up until the</span>
  <span id="freeText16868295942971045289" style="display:none">Sigh. As the final Act of an epic storyline, this novel was, in a word, disappointing.<br /><br />Plot-wise, it was anticlimactic, and utilized a literary device I particularly dislike: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[setting up the climax, and then cutting away to the POV of another character, who arrives on the scene only to witness the aftermath. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Character-wise, I enjoyed the character of Stef, but felt he lacked depth. The interactions between him and Vaneyl were well written, and believable, up until they arrived at the kyree caves. At that point, too much much was glossed over in the haste to get on to the climax. It felt hurried and incomplete.<br /><br />I did enjoy the story, however. I just wish it left me feeling more satisfied than hollow.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YBGPFAYw40jV3zsmssvsCBKuSXQMIM7LK3M7ET18dOcA08/PJ1bjy2VIGFC1jO9xod3yBumkQp2AlzW4KHh8Zg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gQ+xhmiJN5Yo6S82rTlFn/kyi9lD4DQvSFuSuLDRJQThzfFdSe83FZh+DECqfkbmSkEwq6ZkuHnjv5wRpdUthQ==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8685.Mercedes_Lackey">About Mercedes Lackey</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/8685.Mercedes_Lackey"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1215643156p3/8685.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/8685.Mercedes_Lackey">Mercedes Lackey
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15937542555606229726">Mercedes entered this world on June 24, 1950, in Chicago, had a normal childhood and graduated from Purdue University in 1972. During the late 70's she worked as an artist's model and then went into the computer programming field, ending up with American Airlines in Tulsa, Oklahoma. In addition to her fantasy writing, she has written lyrics for and recorded nearly fifty songs for Firebird Arts & M</span>
  <span id="freeText15937542555606229726" style="display:none">Mercedes entered this world on June 24, 1950, in Chicago, had a normal childhood and graduated from Purdue University in 1972. During the late 70's she worked as an artist's model and then went into the computer programming field, ending up with American Airlines in Tulsa, Oklahoma. In addition to her fantasy writing, she has written lyrics for and recorded nearly fifty songs for Firebird Arts &amp; Music, a small recording company specializing in science fiction folk music.<br /><br />"I'm a storyteller; that's what I see as 'my job'. My stories come out of my characters; how those characters would react to the given situation. Maybe that's why I get letters from readers as young as thirteen and as old as sixty-odd. One of the reasons I write song lyrics is because I see songs as a kind of 'story pill' -- they reduce a story to the barest essentials or encapsulate a particular crucial moment in time. I frequently will write a lyric when I am attempting to get to the heart of a crucial scene; I find that when I have done so, the scene has become absolutely clear in my mind, and I can write exactly what I wanted to say. Another reason is because of the kind of novels I am writing: that is, fantasy, set in an other-world semi-medieval atmosphere. Music is very important to medieval peoples; bards are the chief newsbringers. When I write the 'folk music' of these peoples, I am enriching my whole world, whether I actually use the song in the text or not.<br /><br />"I began writing out of boredom; I continue out of addiction. I can't 'not' write, and as a result I have no social life! I began writing fantasy because I love it, but I try to construct my fantasy worlds with all the care of a 'high-tech' science fiction writer. I apply the principle of TANSTAAFL ['There ain't no such thing as free lunch', credited to Robert Heinlein) to magic, for instance; in my worlds, magic is paid for, and the cost to the magician is frequently a high one. I try to keep my world as solid and real as possible; people deal with stubborn pumps, bugs in the porridge, and love-lives that refuse to become untangled, right along with invading armies and evil magicians. And I try to make all of my characters, even the 'evil magicians,' something more than flat stereotypes. Even evil magicians get up in the night and look for cookies, sometimes.<br /><br />"I suppose that in everything I write I try to expound the creed I gave my character Diana Tregarde in <i>Burning Water</i>:<br /><br />"There's no such thing as 'one, true way'; the only answers worth having are the ones you find for yourself; leave the world better than you found it. Love, freedom, and the chance to do some good -- they're the things worth living and dying for, and if you aren't willing to die for the things worth living for, you might as well turn in your membership in the human race." <br /><br />Also writes as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2504886.Misty_Lackey" rel="nofollow noopener">Misty Lackey</a><br /><br /><a href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/mercedeslackey" rel="nofollow noopener">Author's website</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15937542555606229726" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
